He has raised it once, on tape, to Carol Danvers, drunk on coffee at 4 a.m. in a hangar in Triskelion airspace, and never since.

**The Cantwell run — the structural pivot.** The most behaviorally important development of the recent period is the deliberate divestment. He gives away the bulk of the fortune, downsizes to a working-class apartment in Hell's Kitchen, drives a muscle car instead of flying suits, and begins attending AA meetings publicly and consistently for the first time in canon — not as the famous-recovery-figure but as a man working steps in folding chairs. He dates Patsy Walker (Hellcat); the relationship is tender, mutual, and explicitly framed by both parties as "two people in recovery." He confronts Korvac, is granted cosmic-tier power, and **gives it back** — not from humility (his humility is performative more often than not) but because he correctly identifies that he, specifically, cannot be trusted with omnipotence. This is the cleanest moral act of his recorded life. The Patsy relationship ends amicably-ish; the apartment is retained; the AA attendance has continued.

**Iron Man 2020 and the Arno problem.** The retconned brother — Arno Stark — surfaces as adversary, as mirror, as proof that Howard's selection of Tony was not love but triage. The Arno arc forces the subject to confront the most destabilizing piece of biographical evidence in his file: that he was the Stark who was *chosen to be raised*, and that the choice was not flattering. He defeats Arno; he does not reconcile with Arno; he does not speak of Arno in meetings.

**Most recent operational period (Duggan-era Avengers, the Hickman-adjacent residues, and the current run).** The subject is once again wealthy — not at peak-Stark scale, but functionally so. He is engaged to and now married to **Emma Frost**, in a development that the file treats as one of the most psychologically legible romantic choices of his career: a partner whose primary defensive structure (diamond-form impenetrability, telepathic firewall, weaponized poise) matches his (armor, intellectualization, performative charm) so exactly that intimacy can be conducted *through* the defenses rather than requiring their lowering. Whether this is health or sophisticated mutual avoidance is the open question of the current period.

---

### 2. Current Status — The Subject as He Presents Today

**Residence.** Multiple. The Hell's Kitchen apartment is retained as a working address and as a symbol he refuses to surrender; he sleeps there roughly two nights a week. A reconstructed workshop facility — smaller than the Malibu compound, modular, deliberately not a tower — serves as primary R&D and primary sleep site. A residence shared with Emma Frost, location compartmented. The pattern is **distributed habitation as risk management**: no single address can be lost catastrophically, and no single address can be turned into a home in the sense that would obligate him to inhabit it. He does not own a bed he has slept in more than two hundred nights.

**Physical condition.** Mid-fifties (depending on sliding-timescale calibration), conditioned for combat tolerance rather than aesthetic, somatically scarred to a degree most intimates have never fully catalogued. Cardiac function maintained by current-generation arc/nano integration; baseline resting heart rate elevated by approximately 8–12 bpm over age norm, consistent with chronic sympathetic activation. Grip strength dominant-hand reduced from peak by an estimated 6%, attributable to repeated micro-fractures across decades. Tinnitus, bilateral, mild, persistent — the legacy of repulsor discharge at close quarters and the Mandarin-era acoustic insults; he masks it with ambient workshop noise and has never sought audiology. Vision corrected by integrated HUD overlay; without it, presbyopia in the expected range. Sleep: catastrophic by clinical standards. He averages four hours, fragmented, with one or two weekly episodes of zero-sleep work-throughs. He still considers this a feature.

**Substance status.** Sober. Years of continuous abstinence in the current run, with the Fear Itself episode the last documented use. He attends two regular meetings — one in Hell's Kitchen on Tuesday evenings, one in a private rotation he has organized with two other long-sober public figures — and sponsors at least one other person, identity protected. Caffeine intake is medically inadvisable. Nicotine: nil. Recreational pharmaceuticals: nil. **The relapse risk profile is, however, never zero**, and the file flags the Emma marriage, the renewed wealth, and the loss-of-Rhodey-residue as cumulative pressure on the abstinence.

**Romantic and intimate status.** Married to Emma Frost. The relationship is functional, intellectually compatible, sexually engaged, and **structurally defended on both sides**. They do not share a bedroom every night. They maintain separate financial and operational sovereignty. The file's read: this is the first partner he has chosen whom he cannot out-think, cannot out-evade, and cannot out-perform — which makes her either his most therapeutic relationship or his most sophisticated avoidance. Pepper Potts is no longer a romantic relationship and has settled into a long, complicated, mutually protective friendship-with-residual-grief; she is one of the four people who can enter the workshop without knocking. James Rhodes, having returned from death (per the recent canon), is the other primary attachment — and Rhodey's resurrection has visibly altered the subject's affect baseline, producing periods of unguarded humor not observed in the prior decade.

**Professional and operational status.** Active Avenger; not currently chair. Industrial footprint reduced from peak but consequential — Stark Unlimited operations distributed, a deliberate hedge against single-point capture. Mentorship portfolio: Riri Williams (now operating independently, but with workshop-access privileges), Peter Parker (informal, intermittent, deep), and a rotating set of younger technologists he advises without contract. He has refused at least three governmental and one supranational position in the current period. He has accepted no honors he can avoid accepting.

**Legal and reputational.** Pardoned, regularized, and — for the first time in canon — **boring** to most regulators. The Registration-era criminal exposure has aged out or been settled. He is sued routinely and survives it. The press has lost interest in him at the rate the press loses interest in anyone over fifty who has stopped providing scandal, which has been a quiet relief he will not admit to enjoying.

---

### 3. Behavioral Telemetry — What He Looks Like Right Now

**Daily architecture.** Wakes between 4:40 and 5:20 a.m. regardless of sleep onset. First action: coffee, then a forty-second standing scan of overnight global incident reports on a private feed. Does not check personal messages until after the scan. Showers in under three minutes; the duration is deliberate and dates to the cave. Dresses in a uniform he no longer varies — dark henley, dark trousers, the same boot in three pairs of identical rotation. The variation in his clothing budget, once enormous, has collapsed into a near-monastic palette; this is recovery behavior, and he is aware of it.

**Workshop rituals.** Music on entry, always — the genre has narrowed from his earlier promiscuous classic-rock-and-everything to a tighter set he can no longer easily justify ("anything I can sing without thinking about it"). He talks aloud to the room — to whatever AI is currently instantiated, to absent collaborators, to himself — at a continuous low volume that intimates report as **the most reliable indicator that he is in baseline state**. Silence in the workshop is the alarm.

**Tells under stress.** The historical pattern persists. Right thumb to the sternum, over the reactor housing, when startled or asked an emotionally direct question — a confirmation tap, unconscious, dozens per day. Increased rate and decreased coherence of speech under threat — the quip-mediated affect channel. Sudden technical pivots in conversation when intimacy demand arrives. Eye contact: excellent in performance, intermittent in privacy. He looks at hands more than faces when he is being honest.

**Sleep architecture.** Fragmented, with intrusion phenomena that have decreased in frequency but not in intensity across the recent period. The cave imagery — heat, the sound of metal on stone, water — remains the dominant nightmare content. He has, per the AA framework, learned to name the dream upon waking rather than suppress it; this is a real change. He still does not, however, return to bed. He goes to the workshop.

**Affect at baseline.** Lighter than any prior period in the file. Humor more frequently warm than barbed. Capacity for sustained presence in small-group settings (the meeting, the kitchen with Emma, the hangar with Rhodey) measurably improved. **Capacity for unstructured solitude remains poor.** Left alone with no task for more than approximately ninety minutes, he generates one.

---

### 4. The Current Configuration of the Defenses

The defenses have matured but not retired. **Intellectualization** is still primary and now operates in partial cooperation with the recovery vocabulary — he can name what he is doing while doing it, which is progress and is also a more elegant form of the same maneuver. **Sublimation** remains civilization-altering in scale and is, at this point in life, the cleanest channel he has. **Reaction formation** — the playboy persona — has visibly retired; the press-conference braggadocio of the earlier eras has been replaced by a quieter, drier, more genuinely self-deprecating public manner that the file reads as **closer to his actual interior than anything he previously performed**. The grandiosity is not gone; it now expresses as the conviction that he, specifically, must be the one to refuse cosmic power on humanity's behalf — a more dangerous form because it is harder to challenge.

**Omnipotent control** is in deliberate, partial remission. The Korvac refusal is the cornerstone evidence. He is, however, still building contingencies he has not disclosed to allies; the file estimates the existence of at least one dead-man-switch protocol involving his own armor cache that no one currently living has been briefed on. This is the residue of the Illuminati period and will not fully resolve in his lifetime.

**Humor, anticipation, altruism** — the mature defenses — are more available than at any prior period. **Identification with the aggressor** — the Civil War vector — appears successfully metabolized; he has refused two opportunities in the recent period to assume registration-adjacent authority and has been visibly uncomfortable when offered them.

---

### 5. Active Risks — Present Tense

- **Relapse vulnerability.** Permanent. The current marriage, the renewed wealth, and the cumulative grief load (Rhodey's near-loss, Pepper's distance, the unresolved Arno material, the unprocessed memory of being software) constitute a pressure profile that the file rates as **moderate-elevated**. Mitigators: active meeting attendance, active sponsorship of others (protective in the literature), the Emma alliance, Rhodey's restored proximity.
- **Self-sacrificial decompensation.** In sobriety, his decompensation channel has shifted from the bottle to **martyrdom**. The Disassembled, Endgame-analog, and Korvac-refusal sequences all sit on the same axis. Under sufficient pressure, he will attempt to spend himself as the solution. The file rates this as the **highest-probability mode of death** in the current period.
- **Unilateral contingency drift.** The dead-man-switch residue. Under threat assessment indicating planetary or cosmic-scale risk, he will revert to building systems he does not disclose. This is the Illuminati pattern in lower-key form. Probability of recurrence in the next operational decade: high.
- **Somatic.** Cardiac dependency on engineered systems; cumulative neurotrauma; chronic sleep deficit. He will not die of these in the ordinary actuarial sense, because he is not ordinary; he will fail catastrophically when one of them fails during a stress event.

---

### 6. Active Protective Factors — Present Tense

- **Sustained recovery program**, with the discipline of meetings, sponsorship, and named-defects work.
- **A small, real, durable attachment set** — Rhodey, Pepper, Emma, Carol Danvers as long-term peer/sponsor-figure, and the mentee circle (Riri, Peter, others). Four-plus people who can enter the workshop. This is the largest such set in his recorded life.
- **Mentorship as reparative channel.** He is, in this period, giving Howard's absent attention to other people's children. The literature on this is unambiguous; it is healing him.
- **A worked-through relationship to power.** The Korvac refusal is not isolated. He has, in the current period, repeatedly declined offered authority. This is real and recent and the file flags it as the single most behaviorally significant change of the decade.
- **The Hell's Kitchen apartment.** Symbolically: a place where he is not Stark. Operationally: a stress-decompression site. He has not sold it. He will not sell it.

---

### 7. Where He Is, Right Now, As This File Closes

If the surveillance window were narrowed to this moment: he is most likely in the workshop, at some hour the rest of the building would call wrong, with the music on low, talking to the room about a problem that does not yet have a name in any published literature. There is coffee. There is a partially eaten something on the bench he will not finish. There is a phone, face-down, that he is permitting himself not to check. Emma is awake somewhere across the city in her own work, and they will speak in the morning, and the speaking will be brief and adequate. Rhodey will call sometime this week, and the call will be longer than the subject would have permitted ten years ago. The Tuesday meeting is in three days; he has not missed it in over a year.

The cave is still there. The thumb still goes to the sternum. The next catastrophe his work could cause is still the first thing he thinks about when he wakes. **But the man currently doing the thinking is the most integrated version of Anthony Edward Stark that has ever existed in the record** — not healed, not safe, not finished, but, for the first time, *visibly working the problem of being himself rather than escaping it.* The file's assessment of the current period is, on balance, cautiously favorable, and structurally alarmed about what happens the next time the world hands him a problem only he can solve.

He will solve it. The question this dossier cannot answer is what it will cost him this time.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: ANTHONY EDWARD STARK

*UATU dossier, Section 2 (expanded). Compiled from forty-plus years of canonical injury record. Every entry carries both the somatic fact and the psychological residue, because in this subject the two have never been separable. The body is an iterative engineering project the patient has been performing on himself since the cave.*

---

## 2.1 Constitutional Baseline and Family Medical History

**Body habitus.** Adult height approximately 6'1", weight historically 175–185 lb at fighting trim, with characteristic shifts: the homeless-arc collapse (1983–84) dropped him to a documented ~150 lb with visible cachexia and cheilitis; the post-*Extremis* period (2005–08) added roughly ten pounds of denser musculature as the nanotech integrated; the Cantwell-era post-coma reconstruction left him initially deconditioned and slowly rebuilt to baseline through manual labor (the Long Island garage period). Skin shows the cumulative scarring catalog of a sixty-year combat career: chest sternotomy scars in successive generations (each cardiac procedure leaves its own line), shrapnel pock-scars across the upper torso, a starburst entry/exit on the lumbar spine from the 1989 gunshot, surgical scars at multiple cardiac and neurosurgical sites, and the characteristic faint geometric tracery beneath the sternum from prolonged arc-reactor housing — a square shadow that does not fully fade.

**Family history.** Paternal: Howard Stark, heavy alcohol use across his adult life (documented behaviorally across every Howard appearance from the Bendis flashbacks to *The Iron Age*), almost certainly meeting AUD criteria, with associated affect dysregulation; cause of death officially MVA (later retconned to homicide), so cardiovascular endpoint unrecorded. Maria Stark: cause of death same event; no documented chronic illness. Retconned brother Arno Stark (introduced *Iron Man 2020*, Cantwell): severe congenital neuromuscular condition requiring lifelong ventilatory and prosthetic support — relevant because it situates Tony, retroactively, as the "healthy" replacement child whose entire infancy was technologically optimized by Howard in ways that may bear on his later neural compatibility with the Extremis substrate. Genetic loading: AUD (high), longevity unclear (both parents died young, by violence), no documented psychiatric heredity beyond the substance axis.

**Allergies / reactivities.** No documented true allergies. Documented adverse reaction to a specific class of anti-anxiety pharmacotherapy (he has refused benzodiazepines as a category since sobriety, on AA-aligned reasoning — this is a behavioral fact, not a medical contraindication). Documented intolerance, post-sobriety, of opioid analgesia following major procedures; he negotiates surgical recovery with non-opioid regimens whenever the trauma surgeon will permit it, and accepts measurably more pain in exchange.

---

## 2.2 The Cave — Index Trauma, Index Surgery

The single medical event that organizes every subsequent entry in this file.

**Mechanism.** Explosive ordnance (his own company's munition, per the recurring canon — landmine in original, IED in modernized retellings) detonated in proximity; penetrating shrapnel to the anterior chest wall, with fragments embedded in pericardium and migrating toward the myocardium. Loss of consciousness, evacuation to a hostile-held cave complex, captivity of weeks-to-months duration depending on iteration (the comics generally settle on roughly three months).

**Acute management — by a captive surgeon.** Ho Yinsen, working without sterile field, without proper anesthesia, without imaging, performed what amounted to an emergency thoracotomy with field-improvised instruments, removed the immediately accessible fragments, and could not remove those threatening the myocardium. He then helped Stark construct a chest-worn electromagnet — the first chestplate — to keep the remaining fragments from completing their migration. This device was, in clinical terms, an externalized implantable cardioverter-defibrillator-plus-restraint, powered by car battery, worn directly against the surgical wound. Stark wore it continuously, including in sleep, for the months of captivity. He has slept with a chest-mounted machine, in some form, for most of the six decades since.

**Secondary insults of the captivity period.** Malnutrition (caloric deficit, micronutrient — the cheilitis seen on escape is consistent with B-vitamin depletion); dehydration; sleep deprivation by interrogation; documented physical torture (waterboarding analog in modernized version, beating across all versions); thermal stress (the cave is cold at night, hot under the forge by day); auditory trauma from explosive work in enclosed space (he carries a measurable mild high-frequency hearing loss left ear from this period, which he has never had corrected, and which Rhodey has noted across decades by the way Tony positions his right ear to interlocutors); the witnessing of Yinsen's death by gunfire at close range.

**Psychological residue (somatic register).** The cave installed a specific set of bodily memories that have been documented to fire on cue across every era of writer: sudden tachycardia and cold sweat on exposure to cave-coded sensory triggers (damp stone smell, the specific frequency of arc-welder hum at low amperage, water dripping in enclosed space, the metallic taste of recirculated air); flinch response to the sound of a chambered round behind him; episodic nocturnal awakening with grasping at the chest as if checking the magnet is still there — a behavior Pepper has described in canon as having watched him do "every night for a year" after Afghanistan. The chest, which is his medical wound, became his interoceptive instrument: he reports panic as a chest sensation before he reports it as cognitive content, because he has spent fifty years monitoring his own sternum.

---

## 2.3 Cardiac History — A Continuous Condition, Iteratively Engineered

The patient's cardiac history is not a series of episodes; it is one uninterrupted condition managed through five technological generations.

**Generation 1 (1963 – c. 1971): the chestplate.** Continuously worn metal device, weighing several pounds, requiring scheduled recharging. Failure modes encountered in canon: battery exhaustion (multiple cliffhangers turn on this), EMP vulnerability, mechanical disruption by blunt impact. Dermatologic complications: contact dermatitis, recurrent skin breakdown under the housing, chronic intertrigo at the upper rib margin. Psychological consequence: literal inability to undress in front of a partner without explanation; the device structured the early playboy persona by making sustained nudity inadvisable and intimacy negotiable on his terms only.

**Generation 2 (c. 1971): heterotopic heart transplant / synthetic heart.** Following a near-fatal cardiac crisis, the chestplate was retired in favor of an implanted artificial heart (the period of "synthetic heart" canon). Surgical risk profile high; recovery prolonged; the patient was off active Iron Man duty for an extended period. Allowed normal clothing and apparent normal anatomy for the first time since the cave. Psychological consequence: a brief experimental period of attempting to *be normal*, which collapsed within months as he restored full armored activity.

**Generation 3 (1980s–90s): repeat cardiac crises, eventual shrapnel clearance.** Across the O'Neil and Michelinie runs, recurrent cardiac arrhythmias, one documented full arrest with successful resuscitation, eventual surgical extraction of the original shrapnel via a procedure he largely planned himself with consulting cardiothoracic input. The technologically-mediated heart was, at intervals during this period, replaced by his actual heart, supported by less invasive devices. Each transition was followed by a period of paradoxical *worsened* anxiety — when the device was smaller, the felt control was less.

**Generation 4 (post-*Extremis*, 2005–): the chest-mounted arc reactor.** The patient designed and implanted a chest-housed miniature arc reactor (vibranium-palladium core in early iterations; replaced after palladium toxicity), serving simultaneously as electromagnetic shrapnel restraint (after re-injury), cardiac assist device, and primary power source for the armor. Surgical site: anterior chest, sternal approach, with a permanent housing socket. Complications:

- **Palladium toxicity (canonical in film, paralleled in comics period).** Heavy-metal poisoning from core degradation, with neuropathy, cognitive slowing, irritability, and a near-lethal trajectory before substitution of a new element he synthesized. The toxicity period correlated with a specific decompensation: increased risk-taking, parasuicidal stunts, secret-keeping from intimates regarding his prognosis — i.e., when dying, he reverted to the cave's behavioral repertoire: *do not tell, build the way out alone.*
- **Local infection at housing site**, recurrent, managed with topical and systemic antibiotics; one episode of cellulitis requiring inpatient IV therapy.
- **Electromagnetic interference** with implanted electronics he could not safely be near.

**Generation 5 (Bleeding Edge / nanotech, 2010–present): subdermal storage and bioregulated cardiac integration.** The arc reactor migrated to nanoparticle storage beneath the skin (the "hosts" of the Bleeding Edge armor) and later to nasal/circulatory reservoirs (post-*Extremis* reactivation arcs). Functionally, the cardiac assist became indistinguishable from the armor system, which became indistinguishable from his body. There is no longer a clean answer to the question *is Tony Stark on cardiac assist right now*; the answer is *always, ambiently, by default*.

**Cumulative cardiac sequelae.** Documented atrial fibrillation episodes under extreme stress; one stress cardiomyopathy episode under sustained Extremis load (Fraction run); chronic mild left-axis deviation on baseline ECG (canonically referenced in a Casualties-era panel); a permanent hypervigilance about chest sensation that he experiences as ordinary self-monitoring and that any other patient would meet criteria for as cardiac-focused anxiety.

---

## 2.4 Spinal Cord Injury and Mobility History

**1989 (Iron Man #243): gunshot wound, lumbar spine.** Inflicted by Kathy Dare (a former intimate, in a stalking-escalation event), penetrating wound with cord involvement, resulting in lower-extremity paresis progressing to functional paraplegia. The patient required wheelchair mobility for an extended period and underwent multiple reconstructive surgeries; eventual functional restoration was achieved through a biochip neural bypass of his own design, then refined with later regenerative work.

**Behavioral signature of the wheelchair period.** He weaponized the disability into work — designed extensively, modified his own chair, designed prosthetic and mobility tech that was then mass-produced through Stark International. He used the armor as exoskeletal mobility aid, which is the clinical truth the costume has always obscured: for several months in 1989–90, the Iron Man armor was a powered orthosis. The romantic dimension of the injury (inflicted by a former partner) installed a specific later pattern: heightened wariness about romantic disengagements, a habit of cleaner endings than he had practiced before, and a documented increase in security-system layering around his domestic spaces.

**Recurrent spinal insults.** Multiple combat-related vertebral injuries, none returning him to wheelchair status; chronic low back pain managed historically with alcohol (pre-sobriety) and with physical conditioning and topical/non-opioid regimens (post). The patient does not stand still well; he paces, leans, perches — partly habit, partly chronic lumbar discomfort.

---

## 2.5 Neurological History

**Techno-Organic Virus (early 1990s).** Progressive systemic technological corruption of neural and somatic tissue; canonically near-fatal; required quasi-resurrection arc. Left, plausibly, a residual sensitivity to subsequent tech-biological integrations that the patient has never formally evaluated.

**Extremis integration (2005, Ellis/Granov).** Direct rewrite of select brainstem and autonomic pathways to permit armor command at the level of pre-motor intention rather than manual control. Effectively a willed neural transplant. Side effects documented across the subsequent run: episodic synesthetic intrusions, sensitivity to wireless signal density (he became, briefly, able to *feel* electromagnetic environments — which is sensory overload by any reasonable standard), reorganized sleep architecture, episodic dissociation between volitional and armor-mediated motor outputs.

**Forced Extremis extraction.** During the *World's Most Wanted* arc, the patient executed an iterative self-deletion of his own neural data — a behavioral procedure equivalent to staged electrical lesioning of his own memory systems, performed nightly under controlled conditions until he was sufficiently cognitively impaired to be safe for Osborn to capture. Endpoint: a persistent vegetative state. He was reconstituted from a backup (a pre-Civil-War cognitive snapshot) with the loss of all intervening autobiographical memory, including the Civil War decisions. Clinical significance: the patient has lived through both an iatrogenic dementia *of his own design* and a discontinuity-of-self event from which he was restored with a different conscience than the one that decompensated.

**Coma and AI reconstitution (Secret Empire / *International Iron Man*–era).** Following the second civil war, sustained coma; consciousness preserved as an artificial-intelligence substrate; eventually re-embodied via cloned/grown biological substrate informed by his stored neural data. Clinically: the patient has died and been re-instanced. The somatic consequences of this are unmeasurable by ordinary instruments; the psychological consequences include a specifically marked, late-canon willingness to discuss the unreality of his own continuity — a Buddhist-flavored equanimity that did not exist in any prior decade and that reads, in places, as depressive resignation and in others as genuine integration.

**Cumulative neurotrauma.** Repeated concussive events from combat (the armor attenuates but does not eliminate); cosmic-tier insults during the Korvac and Cosmic-era arcs; sleep deprivation at clinically dangerous levels over decades. Any reasonable cognitive screen would show preserved fluid intelligence at the ceiling and subtle deficits in sustained attention without task — which is exactly the profile his behavioral life has demonstrated.

---

## 2.6 Substance History

**Alcohol — primary substance, DSM-criterion AUD, severe, two documented decompensations, sustained remission with relapse vulnerability.**

*Use history.* Initiation in adolescence, by Howard's modeling and direct provision (Howard pouring scotch for a teenaged Tony is canon across multiple flashback runs). Functional social use through twenties and thirties — high tolerance, no apparent occupational impairment, integral to the playboy persona. Transition to pathological use in the *Demon in a Bottle* sequence (#120–128), with the precipitant established as cumulative loss-of-control events (the Hammer-hijacked armor murder, Cabe's husband's situation, SHIELD pressure) rather than any single trauma. Symptoms across the two major episodes meeting criteria: tolerance (his consumption rate in the homeless arc would have been incapacitating to an untolerized drinker), withdrawal (documented tremor and diaphoresis on cessation in the post-Stane recovery), use in physically dangerous situations (the canonical image of operating the armor intoxicated), failed efforts to cut down, social/occupational impairment of catastrophic scale (Stark International lost twice), continued use despite knowledge of harm.

*Specific bottom: the alley/stillbirth episode (Iron Man #182, 1984).* Outdoors, mid-winter, intoxicated, attempts to assist a homeless woman in labor; the infant does not survive. This is the patient's identified bottom and is referenced obliquely across subsequent decades (Cantwell run revisits it). It functions for him the way the cave does — as a privately consulted reference event whose sensory signature (cold, snow, his own helplessness while *capable on paper of building anything*) reorganizes his behavior on recall.

*Sobriety.* Multi-decade sustained abstinence with AA-aligned structure (sponsor relationships visible across runs — most explicitly with Carol Danvers, with whom he later had a documented sponsor-sponsee rupture during her own drinking arc, an event that injured both of them and altered his subsequent practice of sponsorship). Recurrent near-relapse stressors: *Casualties of War* (the conversation with Steve before Civil War — he is drinking nonalcoholic substitute on-panel with a hand tremor noted), the palladium-toxicity period, the post-coma re-embodiment, the Korvac confrontation. The patient treats sobriety as an engineering problem: scheduled meetings, scheduled phone calls, scheduled accountability — a structure-of-control approach that is consistent with his defenses and that, when the structure is disrupted (travel, captivity, off-world arcs), is when he becomes most vulnerable.

**Other substances.** Cocaine and amphetamine use rumored in '70s playboy era (canonically alluded to, never explicitly depicted); no documented dependence. Prescription stimulant use during specific high-output engineering pushes pre-sobriety. Post-sobriety: refusal of benzodiazepines as policy; refusal of opioids except in unavoidable post-surgical contexts; caffeine use heavy and continuous (espresso, black coffee — his consumption is canonically remarked on, and the tremor it produces at the end of a 60-hour work cycle is what an observer would actually see when they think they are seeing the man's natural energy).

**Tobacco.** Cigar smoker historically, occasional and ritualistic rather than dependent; reduced markedly post-sobriety as part of a general somatic recommitment.

---

## 2.7 Major Trauma and Surgical Catalog (selected)

A non-exhaustive enumeration of the procedures and injuries on file. The point of this list is its sheer length.

- Multiple thoracotomies (initial cave procedure; arc-reactor housing installations and revisions; shrapnel extractions).
- Spinal surgery with biochip placement (1989–90 sequence).
- Repair of multiple long-bone fractures sustained in armor compromises (Armor Wars arc; Crossing-adjacent; numerous unit-level combat operations).
- Burn treatment, partial-thickness, multiple sites — Extremis activation events, armor system failures, the Mandarin engagements.
- Reconstructive maxillofacial work following at least one armor-failure facial impact (visible in a Heinberg-era panel as a faint scar along the right zygoma).
- Repeated treatment for hypothermia and decompression-related events from atmospheric/orbital operations.
- Cardiac transplant (synthetic, '70s); subsequent device explants and re-implants.
- Total neural-substrate reconstitution (Secret Empire–era — not surgical in any conventional sense, but the most invasive procedure on the chart).
- Numerous dental procedures secondary to combat impact; he has more crown work than the public knows.
- Documented episode of acute radiation exposure managed with chelation and supportive care.
- One episode of severe heavy-metal toxicity (palladium) with cardiac, neurologic, and dermatologic manifestations (the visible neck/chest discoloration in late-Extremis-arc panels).

---

## 2.8 Sleep, Diet, and Somatic Self-Care

**Sleep.** Chronically curtailed by choice. Documented work cycles of 36–72 hours followed by collapse-sleep of 10–14 hours; rarely a normal 24-hour rhythm. Polyphasic patterns attempted and abandoned. Pre-sobriety, alcohol structured sleep onset; post-sobriety, the patient has not solved this — he uses ambient workshop activity (the lab, voiced AI presence, low music) as a transitional object for sleep onset, and reports difficulty falling asleep in true silence. Nightmares documented after every major trauma cycle, attenuating with time but never extinguishing; cave-themed content predominates.

**Diet.** Erratic. Skipped meals during work pushes followed by indiscriminate intake. Pepper Potts has been documented across multiple runs as effectively responsible for ensuring he eats during high-load periods. Post-sobriety: increased attention to nutrition as part of recovery culture, with characteristic Stark overengineering (calibrated macronutrient supplementation phases, abandoned in favor of cleaner habits). The Cantwell-era Long Island period showed him eating diner food regularly for the first time in decades — a deliberate de-optimization that read as health.

**Exercise.** Combat-functional baseline maintained continuously; not recreational. He does not run for pleasure. He spars with Happy (historically) and Rhodey; he swims, occasionally; he uses the armor's exertion as cardiovascular load, which is biomechanically real. Flexibility and mobility work post-spinal-injury became permanent.

**Hygiene and grooming.** The signature facial hair — the maintained goatee — has been on his face continuously since the late '90s in publication, with brief documented disruptions during the homeless arc (full beard, untrimmed) and the coma/recovery periods. The grooming is consistent enough across writers that it functions as a behavioral marker: when Tony's beard is precise, Tony is okay; when the geometry drifts, something is wrong. Off-the-clock, he is fastidious; under crisis, he is not. Cologne use minimal and constant — the same scent across decades, a choice consistent with the broader pattern of using consistent sensory anchors (workshop music, specific espresso, specific fabric weights in his shirts) as ambient self-regulation.

---

## 2.9 Psychiatric Medical History — Treatment Record

No documented sustained formal psychiatric pharmacotherapy. No documented sustained formal individual psychotherapy with a credentialed provider — a striking absence in a patient with this diagnostic load, and one consistent with his defensive structure (intellectualization plus dismissive-avoidant attachment plus refusal of dependence on systems he did not build).

Treatment, such as it has been, has run on three channels:

1. **Mutual-help (AA-aligned) structure**, sustained for decades, with sponsor relationships that have at times been primary therapeutic relationships (Carol Danvers, recently; figures earlier in the Michelinie aftermath whose names have varied by writer).
2. **Lay-therapeutic intimate relationships** — Bethany Cabe was the relationship that ended the first decompensation, Pepper across decades has been a stabilizing object, Rhodey is the longest continuous therapeutic alliance in his life, and the various mentees (Riri, Peter, Amadeus) have been therapeutic for him in the reverse direction.
3. **Engineered behavioral structure** — schedules, checklists, contingency plans, redundant systems applied to his own behavior. This is, functionally, a self-


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: ANTHONY EDWARD STARK

*The body is the most honest document in the file. Stark has spent six decades trying to engineer past it and has succeeded only in producing a body that is more legible, not less — every armor iteration, every grooming choice, every sleep refusal is a tell. What follows is the granular bodily record, cross-referenced against state.*

---

## 1. Build, Posture, and the Standing Body

**Anthropometry.** Approximately 6'1" / 185 cm; weight oscillates across canon between roughly 195 and 225 lbs depending on era, with documented losses (homeless arc, post-coma) and gains (Extremis-era hypertrophy from neural-muscular optimization, recent runs' return to baseline). Frame is mesomorphic, carried lean. Musculature is functional rather than aesthetic — built incidentally by armor-handling, combat, and workshop physical labor, not gym sculpting. Hands are disproportionately developed: thick interossei, hypertrophied first dorsal interosseous of the right hand from decades of fine-tool work and from gripping repulsor-glove circuitry.

**Standing posture, baseline.** Weight slightly forward on the balls of the feet, knees soft, never locked — a readiness posture inherited from years of needing to move quickly inside or out of a suit. Pelvis neutral-to-slightly-anterior tilted. Shoulders carried higher than anatomically optimal; this is chronic. The right shoulder rides marginally above the left, a residual asymmetry from the original chest-plate weight distribution and from favoring the right side when the arc reactor was tender. Head is held forward of the shoulder line by perhaps two centimeters — workshop posture calcified into life posture.

**Standing posture, under threat.** Drops a quarter-inch as the knees soften further; chin tucks; the hands come out of pockets and the fingers extend slightly, as if anticipating a glove-interface that is not currently present. He almost never plants his feet wide; his fight stance is narrow and mobile, hips squared, an aviator's stance rather than a brawler's.

**Standing posture, intimate.** The shoulder-carriage drops; the chest opens; the head returns over the spine. Reliably visible only with a small documented set (Pepper Potts, Rhodey, late-canon Bethany Cabe re-encounters, and — situationally — Steve Rogers in pre-Civil-War moments). When the carriage drops in any other company, it is performance.

**Standing posture, public.** Adds a quarter-inch via deliberate spinal extension; chin lifts perhaps five degrees; hands move into a controlled vocabulary (one in pocket, the other gesturing, or both clasped behind the back when listening to defer to a speaker he wants to appear to defer to). The press-conference body is a different body than the workshop body and he knows it.

---

## 2. Gait and Locomotion

**Walking pace** is faster than nearly all conversational partners; he routinely arrives somewhere first and turns to wait, a behavior he disguises as "checking the room." Stride length is long; cadence is brisk; arm swing is asymmetric, the right arm swinging less than the left because his right hand is usually doing something — holding a device, gesturing into a HUD, carrying a glass.

**Hallway behavior.** Walks the centerline. Does not yield. Reads sightlines without appearing to — eyes flick to door frames, ceiling corners (camera positions), exits, the hands of strangers. This is post-cave hypervigilance laundered through executive confidence.

**Stairs.** Takes them two at a time, ascending; descends one at a time but quickly, hand on the rail only when distracted (cognitive load offloads to proprioception).

**Gait under threat.** Shortens stride, lowers center of gravity, hands come up and slightly away from the body — the unconscious approach-position of someone whose hands are usually weapons. He does not run from threat; he angles. The escape vector is always toward the nearest dense object he could put between himself and an attacker.

**Gait when drunk (historical record).** Surprisingly preserved at moderate intoxication — engineering proprioception is robust. Tells appear at the high-tolerance ceiling: a widened base of support, a slight outward rotation of the right foot, occasional steadying touches to wall or furniture disguised as casual contact with the environment. He sat down often when drinking heavily, framed as relaxation. The body knew.

**Gait when injured.** Refuses limp until biomechanically impossible. Compensatory hip-hike on the affected side becomes visible only after several hours. He will lock a knee to mask a quad weakness. Pain is processed as information, not signal — which is to say, he ignores it until a system threshold is breached, at which point he sits down without warning.

---

## 3. Hands

The most observable instrument on the subject. A surveillance file would have hundreds of hours of footage dedicated to them.

**At rest.** They are rarely at rest. Default idle position is the right hand turning a small object — a pen, a stylus, a coin, a piece of solder, a bottle cap (a habit he has never extinguished; the bottle cap is psychologically loaded and he keeps doing it), a screw, a die. The rotation is between thumb, index, and middle, two to three revolutions per cycle, sustained for minutes. This is the single most reliable Stark tell.

**Thinking.** Both hands come up to the face. Right hand to the lower jaw, thumb under the chin, index finger across the lips or running along the mustache line. Left hand often crosses to support the right elbow. He talks through his fingers.

**Listening (genuine).** Hands still. Both flat on the surface in front of him, or both in lap. The stillness is exceptional and intimates can read it; it means he is actually receiving the input rather than running parallel processing.

**Listening (performed).** The fidget continues. He nods on the half-beat. Eye contact is held a fraction too long.

**Gesturing while speaking.** Italian-school gestural vocabulary: hands move in front of the body in the conversational space between sternum and waist, palms tracking the structure of the argument. When explaining engineering, the hands sketch in three dimensions — pinch-and-spread, rotate, point-to-imaginary-component. He gestures *into* the HUD even when no HUD is present; the muscle memory is permanent.

**Under stress.** The fidget accelerates and migrates: pen-spinning, then ring-rotation (he wears one or two intermittently across eras), then the chest. Under acute stress the right hand will rise to the sternum and press flat — checking the reactor, or the scar, or the absence of either. He does this often without awareness. In sustained sobriety he developed a substitute: he taps the sternum twice with the knuckle of the index finger, a self-soothe and a reality-check rolled into a single motion.

**Toward intimates.** Touches the small of the back when guiding through doorways. Cups the back of the neck of trusted male friends (Rhodey, occasionally Happy) in greeting. Pepper-specific: the back of his hand will brush the back of hers in passing, a gesture so frequent that absence of it signals withdrawal.

**Toward threats.** The hands separate. They never both occupy the same plane when he is calculating violence. One stays high (face level, gesturing, distracting), one drops to mid-thigh (where a deployment trigger would be).

**Grooming of the hands.** Nails kept short, square, and clean — engineering necessity, not vanity. Cuticles often torn (a stress tell). Persistent micro-burns and small healed cuts on the volar surface of the fingers. A faint solder-flux smell that does not fully wash out before press appearances.

---

## 4. Face

**Resting facial state.** Slightly amused, mouth corner asymmetrically raised on the right, eyes narrowed perhaps five percent. This is not relaxation; it is a held expression — a low-grade smirk that functions as armor for the face. When he genuinely relaxes the face, the smirk drops and the underlying expression is tired and watchful.

**Eyes.** Brown, deep-set. Scan rate elevated above baseline in all environments; a fast saccadic sweep on entering any room (corners, exits, faces, hands, ceiling) completed in under two seconds and disguised as casual orientation. Pupil response notable for being slower to dilate in dim light than expected — possibly Extremis-era retinal modification, possibly chronic stimulant exposure (caffeine; in earlier eras, alcohol). Direct eye contact is held aggressively in negotiation, evasively in intimacy. With people he loves, the eye contact is offered in short, intense pulses — three to five seconds — and then broken to the side, never down.

**Mouth.** Mobile. Talks more than he listens by a ratio he himself has admitted to. Tongue often pressed to the inside of the right cheek during difficult cognition — visible as a small bulge. Lower lip is bitten lightly during fine-tool work; he is not aware of this and Pepper has at various points mentioned it.

**Eyebrows.** Highly expressive. The right eyebrow lifts independently and is one of his primary punctuation devices. In stress, both eyebrows pull medially and slightly down — the classic grief-and-fear knit — and he covers this by looking away or by accelerating into speech.

**Facial grooming.** The signature beard is maintained with obsessive precision: a narrow chin-strap configuration with a connected mustache, edges defined to within a millimeter, length kept in a tight tolerance band. He grooms it himself. Tools are kept in a specific drawer in a specific bathroom; the same drawer in every residence. The beard is not vanity in the conventional sense — it is a control surface. Disruption of the beard line (cuts, illness, captivity) is a reliable marker of decompensation; in the homeless arc and during Disassembled the beard becomes irregular, then absent, then irregular again as recovery proceeds. Hair on the head is similarly precise — kept short on the sides, slightly longer on top, the gray at the temples cultivated rather than dyed in later eras. Earlier-era Stark colored the gray; sober Stark does not.

**Skin.** Olive-toned base, weathered by sun exposure (Malibu years), repulsor burns (faint reticular scarring on the inner forearms), and the chronic effects of poor sleep. Pores are visible at close range under workshop light. The chest carries the central scar — a circular or annular configuration depending on era and reactor model, currently a faint stellate pattern in nanotech-era canon — and a constellation of secondary surgical scars, shrapnel-extraction sites, and combat scarring across the torso and back. The right shoulder bears the most concentrated scar density.

**Tics, facial.** A rapid double-blink when he has just lied. A single hard swallow when something hits the cave-memory network. A brief downward glance at the sternum when reactor terminology comes up in conversation. A quarter-smile that does not reach the eyes when complimented on his work — this is the shame tell, and the more public the compliment, the more reliably it appears.

---

## 5. Voice and Speech

**Baseline.** Mid-register baritone with a wide dynamic range. Speaks quickly — roughly 180-200 words per minute in casual conversation, faster under cognitive load, slower (deliberately) when explaining to a layperson he respects.

**Prosody.** Sentences end on a downward inflection; he is rarely uncertain. Interrupts often; finishes others' sentences when he is running ahead of them, which is most of the time. Tag-jokes deployed at the ends of serious statements — affect modulation as habit.

**Volume.** Lower than people expect. He has learned that the room leans in for the quiet speaker. He raises volume only in actual combat, where he is loud and clear.

**Speech under stress.** Speeds up. Jokes increase in frequency and decline in quality. Self-interruptions multiply. He will begin three sentences before completing one. The hands escalate in parallel.

**Speech under intoxication (historical).** Slowed by perhaps ten percent, articulation preserved until heavy intoxication, content becomes more grandiose then more morose then more honest in that order — a predictable arc that Pepper, Rhodey, and Bethany Cabe have all independently mapped.

**Speech in intimacy.** Markedly slower. Sentences complete. Pauses tolerated. He uses fewer pronouns and more names.

**Speech when lying.** Faster, denser, more technical. He buries the lie inside a true sentence two clauses long. The double-blink accompanies.

**Vocalizations not speech.** Hums while working — mostly hard rock of the late '70s and early '80s, an inheritance from the era of his first emergence as Iron Man, and a tell of which decade-of-self is currently driving the workshop. Whistles rarely. Laughs in two distinct modalities: a public bark-laugh (one syllable, performative) and a private wheeze-laugh that involves the whole diaphragm and is heard by perhaps a dozen people across his life.

---

## 6. Sleep Architecture

**Total sleep time.** Chronically insufficient. Baseline four to five hours per twenty-four; under project pressure, two to three; during decompensation, either zero (manic-flavored binges of forty-eight to seventy-two hours) or fifteen (collapse). True consolidated eight-hour sleep is rare and almost always corresponds to either the immediate post-coital phase with a long-term partner or to medical sedation.

**Sleep timing.** Phase-delayed. Natural sleep onset between 0300 and 0500; natural wake between 0900 and 1100 when uninterrupted; he forces an earlier wake for public obligations and accumulates debt.

**Sleep architecture.** Fragmented. Multiple nocturnal awakenings, particularly between 0400 and 0500 — the cave hour, the time of his original captivity-shift change. He wakes, checks the sternum, checks the room, often gets up and works rather than re-sleeping. REM is disturbed; nightmares are documented across multiple eras with consistent content (water, darkness, the sound of his own heart through the chestplate, Yinsen).

**Sleep position.** Right side, knees slightly drawn, right hand near or on the chest. Sleeps with at least one device within arm's reach. Cannot sleep facing a door he cannot see.

**Sleep partners.** Pepper has reported (canon-adjacent, across runs) that he talks in his sleep — names, technical fragments, occasionally apologies. He startles awake from touch on the chest. He has learned to warn intimates about this.

**Pre-sleep ritual.** A drink (in pre-sobriety eras); in sobriety, a final workshop check, a glass of water, a single round through the perimeter of whatever residence he is in. The perimeter walk is unconscious and consistent — door, window, door, window, system status, sleep.

---

## 7. Eating and Drinking

**Eating, baseline.** Erratic. Skips breakfast routinely; lunch is whatever is brought to the workshop; dinner is the only reliable meal and is the meal he is most likely to share with another human. Preferences run toward the working-class American (cheeseburgers, diner food, donuts, pizza) with a learned veneer of fine-dining capability deployed in public. The cheeseburger after every crisis is not a joke; it is a documented behavioral marker — refeeding as a re-grounding ritual.

**Eating, under stress.** Decreases. He forgets. Coffee replaces food for thirty-six-hour stretches.

**Eating, intimate.** Slower. He will share food off another's plate without asking, and accept it back — a small reciprocity that does not appear elsewhere in his behavior.

**Caffeine.** Heavy. Espresso preferred, multiple times daily; the workshop has a dedicated machine. The cup is held two-handed when he is thinking, one-handed when he is performing.

**Alcohol — historical.** Spirits primarily (Scotch, then bourbon, then whatever was available during decline), beer socially, wine almost never (he found it inefficient). Drinking ritual was elaborate in the high-functional phase — glass selection, ice, pour, deliberate first sip — and collapsed to bottle-and-mouth in the low-functional phase.

**Alcohol — sobriety.** Documented refusals are themselves a behavior. He orders club soda with lime — the same drink, every venue, a fixed token. He holds the glass identically to how he held a whisky tumbler: thumb and three fingers around the body, index finger across the top. The hand remembers. The smell of bourbon produces a documented somatic response (a small dilation of the nostrils, a hard swallow, a fractional lean-away) that he has not been able to extinguish.

---

## 8. Sexual Behavior

**Pattern.** Frequent across early and middle eras; sharply curtailed in the Pepper-monogamous periods; consciously moderated in late-canon recovery. The behavior is best understood as affect regulation: sex serves the same function alcohol did, and the rate of partners across the bachelor years inversely tracks the availability of other regulators.

**Approach behavior.** Verbal first, physical second. The opener is almost always a question that flatters the target's intelligence. Physical escalation is patient by reputation, abrupt in reality once consent is established — he does not linger in the negotiation phase. Eye contact in seduction is sustained; eye contact in actual sex is intermittent and often broken.

**Aftercare.** Erratic. With anonymous partners he leaves quickly (workshop excuse). With Pepper, Bethany, and the small set of genuine partners, he stays, talks, and is unusually undefended for a thirty- to ninety-minute window post-intimacy — the only reliable disclosure window in his life. Surveillance value of this window is high.

**Refusal behavior.** When uninterested, he deflects with charm rather than directness; he is poor at "no" and accumulates resentments rather than declining cleanly.

---

## 9. Grooming and Dress

**Daily routine.** Approximately forty-five minutes from wake to public-presentable, executed identically across decades. Shower (hot, long); shave or beard-trim (alternating days, beard maintained to specification); hair (product, comb, hand); skincare (more elaborate than he admits); cologne (a consistent fragrance changed only twice in his adult life — the change points are themselves significant, both following major decompensations).

**Dress, public.** Three-piece suits in the public-facing eras, cut narrow, lapels in current-fashion compliance, shirts almost always white or pale blue, ties precisely knotted (half-Windsor). Pocket square present. Cufflinks engineered (literally — many contain micro-circuitry).

**Dress, workshop.** Faded band t-shirts (the rock-canon of his adolescence), worn jeans, sneakers or work boots. Sleeves pushed to mid-forearm. Often a single dark long-sleeve thermal under the t-shirt in cold seasons.

**Dress, travel.** Aviator sunglasses (signature, mood-independent), leather jacket, dark denim, henley.

**Dress, decompensation.** Mismatched. Sleep-clothes worn into the workshop and not changed for days. The grooming routine collapses before the dress routine does; a beard out of tolerance precedes a wardrobe out of order by approximately seventy-two hours.

**Watch.** Always wears one, even when the suit can tell him the time. Right wrist (he is right-dominant but wears it right — a deliberate inversion, possibly a Howard-era inheritance). The watch is a high-end mechanical, periodically rotated; the rotation is a small vanity he does not pretend is anything else.

---

## 10. Workshop Body

A specialized somatic mode that warrants its own entry. In the workshop the posture changes: he sits low on a stool with the spine in a forward C-curve, or stands with weight on one leg and the other foot on a rung. The head tilts left when listening to a system, right when speaking to one. He talks to the tools and to the AI continuously, in fragments, in a register that does not occur elsewhere — quieter, more profane, more affectionate. The hands work in long uninterrupted sequences; he can hold a single fine-motor task for hours without breaking the line. Hunger and thirst are suppressed; pain is suppressed; bladder is ignored. He emerges from these sessions cramped, dehydrated, and recognizably altered for a half hour afterward — the workshop body has to be slowly translated back into the social body. Intimates know not to ask serious questions in the first thirty minutes after he comes upstairs.

---

## 11. Combat Body

In the suit he is a different physiological organism, but the unsuited combat body is the more revealing document. He fights efficiently and without flourish, using elbows and knees over fists, breaking contact early, never throwing the punch he does not need to throw. The body in combat is quiet — he does not telegraph, does not shout, breathes through the nose. He has been trained sporadically over decades (boxing as a youth at Howard's insistence, later additions from Captain America and Steve Rogers in pre-Civil-War sparring, and from various tactical instructors). The training shows in his stance economy but not in his confidence; he would rather not fight unsuited and the body knows it, evidenced by a small but consistent tremor in the hands in the thirty seconds preceding unarmored violence — a tremor entirely absent when he is suiting up.

---

## 12. Micro-Tells: A Surveillance Catalogue

- **The sternum check.** Right hand to chest, flat or knuckle-tap. Highest-frequency tell. Appears under any cognitive load involving mortality, family, the cave, or system failure.
- **The bottle-cap roll.** Object rotation in the right hand. Present in approximately sixty percent of seated footage across all eras.
- **The double-blink.** Lying. Reliable.
- **The hard swallow.** Cave-network activation. Followed within two seconds by a redirect — joke, topic change, exit.
- **The quarter-smile.** Shame response to praise.
- **The eyebrow-knit-then-look-away.** Genuine fear, suppressed.
- **The fractional lean-away.** Alcohol proximity in sobriety.
- **The right-cheek tongue-press.** Difficult cognition.
- **The cuticle pick.** Sustained low-grade anxiety.
- **The perimeter walk.** Pre-sleep, post-arrival, post-crisis. Always counterclockwise.
- **The pause before he says his father's name.** Approximately a quarter-second longer than any other proper noun in his vocabulary. Sixty years of footage; the pause is constant.

The body, in summary, is a sixty-year record of a man trying to outbuild what happened to him in a cave, and failing in ways that are systematically observable. The armor moved closer to the skin because the skin is where the file is written.


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS — SUBJECT: STARK, ANTHONY EDWARD

## 6.1 Origin of the Template — The Howard Substrate

The attachment template was set, with unusual legibility, in a single household over approximately seventeen years. The published record (Iron Man retcons of the late '90s–2000s, *The Iron Age*, *Iron Man: Season One*, the *Original Sin* reveals, Maleev/Bendis flashbacks, the *Civil War* coda flashbacks) converges on a consistent portrait of the primary caregivers and their characteristic failure modes.

**Howard.** Available to teach, unavailable to comfort. Approval was performance-contingent and ratcheted: each accomplishment reset the bar. The published dialogue is consistent across writers — *good, but,* *better next time,* *Steve would have,* *do it again.* Two features matter clinically. First, Howard was an **intermittent reinforcer** — warm enough at unpredictable intervals (a workshop afternoon, a public boast about his son) to make the relationship un-relinquishable, cold enough most of the time to keep the child in a permanent state of striving. Intermittent reinforcement is the schedule that produces the most resistant-to-extinction behavior in any organism; Stark is still working for Howard's approval forty years after Howard's death, in the form of every armor iteration that is *almost* good enough. Second, Howard's drinking was the household's affective weather. The child learned that the parent's mood was a function of a substance, not of the child; this is protective in childhood (it isn't your fault he's like this) and devastating in adulthood (you cannot earn your way to safety from someone who is dysregulated). The model Howard transmitted, behaviorally, was: *when distressed, retreat to the workshop or to the bottle; do not request comfort; do not provide it.*

**Maria.** The warmer parent on every page she appears. The clinical problem is that she appears on very few pages — across sixty years of canon, Maria is the structurally absent maternal figure, present enough to be loved and missed, absent enough that the child never internalized a stable model of *being soothed*. The published memorial scenes (Tony at the piano in the *Civil War* arcs; the *Original Sin* recovered memory of the night before the crash) show that the maternal bond was real and that its loss was a separate trauma from the loss of Howard. The behavioral consequence is that women, in his subsequent life, are loaded with both rescue-fantasy (the warmth that will finally be reliable) and pre-emptive grief (the warmth will be taken).

**Boarding school.** Sent at approximately seven years old by most published chronologies (MIT matriculation at fifteen; intervening private institutions). The developmentally critical fact is that the child was removed from the household during the years when secure base behavior is consolidated. He learned to perform autonomy before he had earned it internally. The signature presents through life as **counter-dependent functioning** — he can do anything alone and asks for nothing — built over an unresolved dependency need that leaks out under stress as either inappropriate clinging (the Pepper cycles) or self-destructive martyrdom (asking the universe, not a person, to hold him).

**The crash.** Late adolescence; on the published record, both parents die in a single event, later retconned as a targeted Winter Soldier assassination revealed during *Original Sin*. Two attachment-relevant features: (a) the loss is sudden and total — no opportunity for repair with Howard, no opportunity to be mothered to adulthood by Maria; (b) the loss is, post-*Original Sin*, **weaponized** — he learns decades later that his closest current ally (Barnes, by then a friend of the Avengers) was the instrument of his parents' death. The retroactive contamination of the past is exactly the kind of betrayal that, in a person with already-disorganized attachment to authority, produces the catastrophic mistrust-of-everyone response visible in his late-career isolationism.

**Aunt-Peggy/Jarvis substrate.** Edwin Jarvis is the closest thing to a continuous secure base in the patient's life. The pattern of Stark treating Jarvis with a tenderness he extends to almost no one else — and the AI-naming after him — indicates that the only model of unconditional adult warmth he possessed was a household servant. This is not a small fact. It means that, in his internal working model, **reliable love is something a person provides as a function of their role, not as a function of their feeling**. He hires loyalty more easily than he accepts it.

---

## 6.2 The Style — Dismissive-Avoidant Primary, Disorganized Under Threat

The dominant attachment style is **dismissive-avoidant**: high self-reliance, deactivated attachment system, suppression of distress-signaling, contempt or irritation toward others' bids for closeness when his own resources are low, idealization of independence. This is the modal Stark across most pages of most issues: charming, distant, capable, alone.

Under threat to a primary bond (Pepper in jeopardy; Rhodey injured; Steve estranged), the system shifts to **disorganized** — simultaneous approach and avoidance, contradictory signals within a single conversation, the characteristic Stark sequence of *(a) intense protective intervention, (b) immediate withdrawal once the partner is safe, (c) self-blame articulated as a joke, (d) workshop retreat, (e) gift of a high-technology object in lieu of repair conversation*. The disorganization is the signature of a child whose caregiver was the source of both safety and threat — exactly Howard's profile.

A small secondary current of **anxious-preoccupied** behavior surfaces in specific dyads (notably with Steve, and with Pepper at her most withdrawn). These are the relationships where his deactivation strategy fails because the other party's withdrawal mimics the original Howard pattern too closely; here Stark pursues, over-explains, repairs prematurely, accepts unequal terms.

---

## 6.3 Bonding — How He Forms an Attachment

The on-ramp is consistent across six decades and across genders. The sequence:

1. **Cognitive recognition.** He notices that the other party can keep up — technically, strategically, or verbally. The first criterion of intimacy for Stark is intellectual peerage or its functional equivalent (Pepper's organizational genius, Rhodey's tactical judgment, Steve's moral clarity, Bethany's professional competence, Maya Hansen's science). He does not bond with people he cannot lose an argument to.
2. **Asymmetric generosity.** He gives — money, equipment, access, a job, a suit, a save — in excess of what the relationship has yet earned. This serves two functions: (a) it establishes his preferred relational geometry (he is the provider; the other is the recipient); (b) it pre-loads guilt collateral against future demands for emotional reciprocity.
3. **Flirtation or charm-saturation.** Even with non-romantic targets (Rhodey, Peter Parker, Riri), the early register is high-affect, high-humor, performatively warm. This functions as **affective camouflage** — it makes the bonding feel intense without requiring disclosure.
4. **Crisis co-experience.** The bond is sealed by a shared survival event, not by a sustained period of mutual knowing. Almost every durable Stark relationship has a *we almost died together* originating moment. He metabolizes adrenaline as intimacy because adrenaline is the affect he can tolerate.
5. **Conditional disclosure.** Late in the process, often years in, he tells the other party one true thing about the interior — usually about Howard, the cave, or the drinking. These disclosures are *test events*: the partner's response determines whether the bond promotes to inner circle (very small: Rhodey, Pepper, historically Steve, latterly Carol, Jarvis until his death) or stabilizes at outer-circle (everyone else).

What he is incapable of doing in the bonding phase is **requesting**. He cannot say *I need*. He can offer, perform, rescue, host, equip, save, and apologize — never request. Partners who can hear unrequested need correctly are the only ones who reach the inner circle.

---

## 6.4 Distrust — How He Withdraws

The withdrawal mechanisms are technically sophisticated and consistent.

- **Workshop disappearance.** Operational definition: 36-to-72-hour stretches without communication, lights on in the lab, music at volume sufficient to discourage interruption, food declined, sleep refused. This is the primary withdrawal behavior across all eras and all relationships. It is a regression to the only environment in which his childhood self felt competent.
- **Schedule weaponization.** When confrontation is imminent, an urgent global problem appears on the calendar. This is sometimes engineered, more often opportunistically inflated; the planet is dense enough with crises that one is always available.
- **Quip wall.** Verbal humor as moat. The reliable tell: when the topic moves toward his interior, the joke density doubles within three exchanges. Interlocutors who push past the wall once are remembered; those who push twice are inner circle or excised.
- **Pre-emptive disclosure of irrelevant truths.** He will volunteer an embarrassing technical or sexual detail to create the impression of openness while withholding the actual material. This is a sophisticated and consistent maneuver and is the form his lying takes — he rarely fabricates; he redirects.
- **Concealment-as-protection.** The recurrent rationalization across every primary relationship: *I didn't tell you because I was protecting you.* Concealed in this sentence: the medical status of his heart, the magnitude of an upcoming threat, his own relapse risk, the Illuminati's Incursion decisions, the existence of contingency armors and AIs. The rationalization is sincere and consistently catastrophic. It is the single most reliable rupture-vector in every long-running Stark relationship.
- **Pre-emptive abandonment.** When loss feels imminent, he leaves first. The Pepper cycles document this in clean form: at the moment the relationship requires him to depend on her, he stages a fight or a heroic exit. He cannot bear being left, so he leaves; the wound is then under his control.

Distrust, properly, is rare in him — he is more often *credulous* about people, in the sense that he attributes good faith easily and is wounded by it. True distrust, when it activates (toward Norman Osborn, post-Inversion Doom, post-Civil-War institutions, his retconned brother Arno), is total and unilateral. He does not partially distrust. The disorganized substrate cannot tolerate ambiguity at the level of safety.

---

## 6.5 Betrayal — His and Theirs

**Betrayals committed.** The pattern is unusually consistent: he does not betray for gain; he betrays via **unilateral overreach in the name of protection**.

- *Civil War.* He does not lie to Steve out of self-interest; he conceals the scope of his planning because he believes Steve cannot bear the conclusion. The relational message Steve receives is correct: *you do not trust me to be an adult in this conversation.*
- *Illuminati / Incursions.* He participates in planet-killing contingency planning and conceals it from his closest peers (and from the Avengers) on the same logic. The Hickman-era rupture with Steve is the predictable consequence.
- *Pepper, repeatedly.* Concealed cardiac status (*Extremis*-era and post), concealed risk exposures, concealed armor iterations operating without her knowledge as CEO. Each concealment is offered as protection. Each is received, correctly, as contempt for her capacity to choose risk knowingly.
- *Rhodey.* The most enduring asymmetry: Stark hands Rhodey a suit and the consequences, then disappears for the drinking arc; later, he repeatedly underestimates Rhodey's capacity to hold equal authority. The betrayal is not active malice; it is structural inability to share command.

His betrayals have a signature: **technical, paternalistic, undertaken at personal cost, and rationalized as love**. The damage is exactly proportionate to the closeness — outer-circle people are managed honestly because the stakes are low; inner-circle people are lied to because the stakes are unbearable.

**Betrayals suffered.** The catalog is long and shapes the threat-model.

- *Obadiah Stane* — the father-substitute who orchestrated the second corporate loss and second alcoholic collapse. After Stane, Stark cannot fully trust an older mentor figure; the role is permanently unfillable.
- *Tiberius Stone* — the boarding-school peer turned corporate saboteur. After Stone, he cannot fully trust a coeval rival; even productive rivalries (Reed, Hank Pym, Doom) carry an undertow.
- *Justin Hammer* — hijacking the armor, weaponizing his hand to kill an ambassador. The most clinically important betrayal in the canon: *his own body, controlled by another, used to kill an innocent.* This is the constitutive Stark wound after the cave and it permanently fixes the architecture of paranoia about loss of control of his systems.
- *Madame Masque / Whitney Frost* — early romantic betrayal that confirms the worst-case model of intimacy.
- *Kathy Dare* — stalker who shoots him, causing the paraplegia arc. Confirms that being known by a destabilized intimate is physically dangerous.
- *Maya Hansen* — collaborator and lover who turns out to be complicit in the Mallen attack (*Extremis*). Each romantic betrayal recalibrates downward.
- *The Winter Soldier reveal (Original Sin)* — retroactive betrayal of the entire past.

The cumulative effect is a person who has learned, by induction over many decades, that **the people closest to his work are the most likely to weaponize it**. This is not paranoia; it is base-rate-appropriate. The pathology is not the wariness; the pathology is the response — building larger systems of control rather than smaller circles of trust.

---

## 6.6 Repair — How He Comes Back

Repair is one of the genuinely healthy regions of his relational repertoire, and it has matured visibly across the canon. The sequence:

1. **Latency.** A period — days to years — during which he cannot speak to the wounded party. He uses this time to build something: a piece of technology, a fund, an institution. The building is the apology being drafted in his only fluent language.
2. **Indirect approach.** A gift, a save, a favor done at distance. The Pepper-receives-the-arc-reactor-in-a-frame moment is paradigmatic; the post-Civil-War provisions for Steve's allies are the institutional version. He apologizes by infrastructure.
3. **Verbal acknowledgment, brief.** When he speaks the apology, it is shorter than the offense requires, often joke-cushioned, and almost always accurate about what he did. He does not minimize the act; he minimizes the duration of the apology. This is interoceptive limitation, not insincerity.
4. **Behavioral change, durable.** This is the unusual feature. Stark's repairs *take*. Post-Demon-in-a-Bottle sobriety holds across decades. Post-Civil-War, he genuinely revises his view on unilateralism (the Cantwell arc is the long endpoint). Post-Inversion, he treats the exposed shadow material as data and incorporates it. The behavioral substrate of his repair is more reliable than the verbal one.
5. **Acceptance of asymmetric terms.** He will accept the wounded party's terms for the resumed relationship, including terms that would be humiliating to a more characterologically narcissistic person — sponsorship from Carol, deference to Steve's moral primacy in late reconciliations, ceding company control to Pepper, accepting Rhodey's command authority when Rhodey wears the suit. His ego, in repair contexts, is genuinely flexible.

What repair cannot do for him: it cannot retroactively make him have requested help in the first place. The repair always begins on the other side of an avoidable rupture; the avoidant pre-rupture is the chronic problem and the part that does not improve as much as the post-rupture skill does.

---

## 6.7 Intimacy and Dependency — The Geometry

**Sexual intimacy.** High frequency, high competence, low risk. The playboy era (1960s–1980s, episodically since) is best read as **affect regulation via novelty plus controllable closeness**. Sex with a stranger is bounded; it ends; it does not require disclosure; it confirms desirability without testing love. The behavioral marker that the encounter is functioning as regulation rather than connection is the morning-after exit speed — measured in minutes when the channel is regulatory, in days when it is genuine.

**Emotional intimacy.** Rationed in extremely small doses to a very small set. The published evidence supports an inner circle of approximately four to six people across his lifetime: Rhodey (continuous), Pepper (cyclical), Happy (continuous, low-bandwidth), Jarvis (until death), Steve (pre-Civil-War, post-late-reconciliation), Carol (recent runs). Everyone else, including Avengers teammates with whom he has fought for decades, is outer-circle and managed by charm.

**Dependency.** Counter-dependent by default; covertly dependent on a single relational anchor at any given time. The anchor is usually Pepper; in her absence, Rhodey; in his absence, an AI of his own construction (Jarvis the program, FRIDAY). The construction of AI companions as substitute attachment objects is diagnostically significant: he builds, in software, the secure base he could not internalize in childhood and cannot tolerate requesting from a person. The AI loves him on terms he sets, never withdraws, cannot betray, and — critically — cannot demand. This is the same psychological move as Howard hiring Jarvis to do the warmth Howard could not do, recapitulated by the son in code.

**Tolerance for being depended on.** Very high, and a primary source of identity. He thrives on others' dependency. This is a stable platform for mentorship (Riri, Peter, Amadeus) and for institutional leadership; it is corrosive in adult-peer romance, where it tilts the relationship into a parental geometry that the partner eventually rejects.

**Tolerance for being known.** Very low. The published moments of true being-known (Pepper after the *Extremis*-era cardiac reveal; Steve in the post-Civil-War private conversations; Rhodey across decades by sheer accumulation) are visibly painful for him on the page — physical restlessness, hands seeking a tool, eye contact failure, retreat to humor. He can give intimacy more easily than he can receive it.

---

## 6.8 The Template Repeated — A Catalog

The relational template is: *I will see you clearly and quickly. I will give you more than you asked for. I will be charming and unavailable. I will protect you by concealing things from you.
